Since I have selected only a few of the samples is possible that some of the OTU's are left with a total abundance of zero. In R it is possible to have functions within functions so the following will print the number of columns in the data set that has a sum equla to 0: 


<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxuYGBgclxubGVuZ3RoKHdoaWNoKGNvbFN1bXMob3R1LnRhYi5zaW1wbGUpPT0wKSlcbmBgYFxuYGBgIn0= -->

```r
```r
length(which(colSums(otu.tab.simple)==0))

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

<!-- rnb-output-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiWzFdIDE0ODNcbiJ9 -->

[1] 1483




<!-- rnb-output-end -->

<!-- rnb-chunk-end -->


<!-- rnb-text-begin -->

We can use the same idea of a function within a function to exclude the OTUs with a total number of 0. 

<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxuYGBgclxub3R1LnRhYi5zaW1wbGU8LW90dS50YWIuc2ltcGxlWywtKHdoaWNoKGNvbFN1bXMob3R1LnRhYi5zaW1wbGUpPT0wKSldXG5gYGBcbmBgYCJ9 -->

```r
```r
otu.tab.simple<-otu.tab.simple[,-(which(colSums(otu.tab.simple)==0))]

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

<!-- rnb-chunk-end -->

Now how many are 0?

## Common metrics and methods

The following calculations uses function in the vegan package written by Jari Oksanen.  
*Vegan is an R package for community ecologists. It contains the most popular methods of multivariate analysis needed in analysing ecological communities, and tools for diversity analysis, and other potentially useful functions*. If you want to learn more about the vegan you can run ```browseVignettes("vegan")```

#Fitting data to the Preston model
preston<-prestonfit(colSums(otu.tab.simple))
preston.dist<-prestondistr(colSums(otu.tab.simple))
plot(preston)
lines(preston.dist, line.col=\blue3\)

<!-- rnb-text-begin -->


### Pielou's index of evenness (range 0-1, 1 = maximum evenness)
`J=H/Hmax`  
`J=Shannon (H) / log(S=species richness)`

<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxuYGBgclxuSiA8LSBIL2xvZyhyb3dTdW1zKG90dS50YWIuc2ltcGxlPjApKVxuYGBgXG5gYGAifQ== -->

```r
```r
J <- H/log(rowSums(otu.tab.simple>0))

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

<!-- rnb-chunk-end -->


<!-- rnb-text-begin -->


### Inverse Simpson's D index (richness+evenness. Larger values, larger diversity)

<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxuYGBgclxuaW52LnNpbXBzb248LWRpdmVyc2l0eShvdHUudGFiLnNpbXBsZSwgXFxpbnZzaW1wc29uXFwpXG5wbG90KGludi5zaW1wc29uLCB0eXBlPVxcbFxcLCBjb2w9XFxibHVlXFwpXG5gYGBcbmBgYCJ9 -->

```r
```r
inv.simpson<-diversity(otu.tab.simple, \invsimpson\)
plot(inv.simpson, type=\l\, col=\blue\)

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

# Beta diversity
We rarefy all samples to the same sequencing depth, to reduce biases

<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxuYGBgclxubWluKHJvd1N1bXMob3R1LnRhYi5zaW1wbGUpKSAjIFdlIGNhbGN1bGF0ZSB0aGUgc2FtcGxlIHdpdGggdGhlIG1pbmltdW0gYW1vdW50IG9mIHJlYWRzXG5gYGBcbmBgYCJ9 -->

```r
```r
min(rowSums(otu.tab.simple)) # We calculate the sample with the minimum amount of reads

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

<!-- rnb-output-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiWzFdIDk5NDZcbiJ9 -->

<!-- rnb-output-end -->

<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxuYGBgclxub3R1LnRhYi5zaW1wbGUuc3M8LXJyYXJlZnkob3R1LnRhYi5zaW1wbGUsIG1pbihyb3dTdW1zKG90dS50YWIuc2ltcGxlKSkpICNTYW1wbGVzIGFyZSByYXJlZmllZCB0byBsb3dlc3QgbnVtYmVyIG9mIHJlYWRzIFxucm93U3VtcyhvdHUudGFiLnNpbXBsZS5zcylcbmBgYFxuYGBgIn0= -->

```r

```r
